      <p><b>Vanuatu</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small>English: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: secondary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ÉË/: 'a' in 'father'">ÉË</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/u/: 'u' in 'influence'">u</span><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="/ÉË/: 'a' in 'father'">ÉË</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/uË/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uË</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Vanuatu.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/En-us-Vanuatu.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Vanuatu.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">VAH</span>-noo-<span style="font-size:90%">AH</span>-too</i></a> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/Ã¦/: 'a' in 'bad'">Ã¦</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ÉË/: 'a' in 'father'">ÉË</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/uË/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uË</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">van-<span style="font-size:90%">WAH</span>-too</i></a>; <small>Bislama and French pronunciation&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[vanuatu]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Vanuatu</b> (French: <i lang="fr">RÃ©publique de Vanuatu</i>; <a href="/wiki/Bislama" title="Bislama">Bislama</a>: <i>Ripablik blong Vanuatu</i>), is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> located in the South Pacific Ocean. The <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a>, which is of volcanic origin, is 1,750 kilometres (1,090&nbsp;mi) east of northern Australia, 540 kilometres (340&nbsp;mi) northeast of <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, and west of <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>. </p>
      <p>Vanuatu was first inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesian</a> people. The first Europeans to visit the islands were a Spanish expedition led by Portuguese navigator <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de QueirÃ³s">Fernandes de QueirÃ³s</a>, who arrived on the largest island, <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADritu_Santo" class="mw-redirect" title="EspÃ­ritu Santo">EspÃ­ritu Santo</a>, in 1606. QueirÃ³s claimed the archipelago for Spain, as part of the colonial <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>, and named it <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">La Austrialia del EspÃ­ritu Santo</i>. </p>
      <p>In the 1880s, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a> claimed parts of the archipelago, and in 1906, they agreed on a framework for jointly managing the archipelago as the <a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides" title="New Hebrides">New Hebrides</a> through an Anglo-French <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">condominium</a>. </p>
      <p>An independence movement arose in the 1970s, and the Republic of Vanuatu was founded in 1980. Since independence, the country has become a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation internationale de la Francophonie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Vanuatu's name derives from the word <i><a href="/wiki/Vanua" title="Vanua">vanua</a></i> ("land" or "home"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHess2009115_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHess2009115-9">[9]</a></sup> which occurs in several <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian languages</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[a]</a></sup> combined with the word <i>tu</i>, meaning "to stand" (from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Oceanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Oceanic">POc</a> *<i>tuqur</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> Together, the two words convey the independent status of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowley20043_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowley20043-12">[11]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Vanuatu" title="History of Vanuatu">History of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The history of Vanuatu before European colonization is mostly obscure because of the lack of written sources up to that point, and because only limited archaeological work has been conducted; Vanuatu's volatile geology and climate is also likely to have destroyed or hidden many prehistoric sites.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> However, archaeological evidence gathered since the 1980s supports the theory that the Vanuatuan islands were first settled about 3,000 years ago, in the period roughly between 1,100 BC and 700 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBedfordSpriggs2008_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBedfordSpriggs2008-14">[13]</a></sup> These were almost certainly people of the <a href="/wiki/Lapita_culture" title="Lapita culture">Lapita culture</a>. The formerly widespread idea that Vanuatu might have been only marginally affected by this culture was rendered obsolete by the evidence uncovered in recent decades at numerous sites on most of the islands in the archipelago, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Banks_Islands" title="Banks Islands">Banks Islands</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Aneityum" title="Aneityum">Aneityum</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Notable Lapita sites include <a href="/wiki/Teouma" title="Teouma">Teouma</a> on <a href="/wiki/%C3%89fat%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="ÃfatÃ©">ÃfatÃ©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uripiv" title="Uripiv">Uripiv</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vao_Island" title="Vao Island">Vao</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Malakula" title="Malakula">Malakula</a>, and Makue on <a href="/wiki/Aore" class="mw-redirect" title="Aore">Aore</a>. Several ancient burial sites have been excavated, most notably Teouma on ÃfatÃ©, which has a large ancient cemetery containing the remains of 94 individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> There are also sites â on Ãfate and on the adjacent islands of <a href="/wiki/Lelepa_Island" title="Lelepa Island">Lelepa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eretoka" title="Eretoka">Eretoka</a> â associated with the 16thâ17th century chief or chiefs called <a href="/wiki/Roy_Mata" class="mw-redirect" title="Roy Mata">Roy Mata</a>. (This may be a title held by different men over several generations.) Roy Mata is said to have united local clans and instituted and presided over an era of peace.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Challenges_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Challenges-16">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The stories about Roy Mata come from local oral tradition, and are consistent with centuries-old evidence uncovered at archaeological sites.<sup id="cite_ref-Challenges_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Challenges-16">[15]</a></sup> The Lapita sites became Vanuatu's first UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RNZI_40819_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RNZI_40819-18">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg/220px-Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg/330px-Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg/440px-Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fels_Cave_Drawings_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cave paintings, <a href="/wiki/Lelepa_Island" title="Lelepa Island">Lelepa Island</a> associated with the <a href="/wiki/Roy_Mata" class="mw-redirect" title="Roy Mata">Roy Mata</a> World Heritage Site
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The immediate origins of the Lapita lay to the northwest, in the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bismark_Archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Bismark Archipelago">Bismark Archipelago</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> though DNA studies of a 3,000 year old skeleton found near <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a> in 2016 indicates that some may have arrived directly from the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, pausing only briefly en route.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> They brought with them crops such as <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>, as well as domesticated animals such as <a href="/wiki/Pigs" class="mw-redirect" title="Pigs">pigs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chickens" class="mw-redirect" title="Chickens">chickens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> Their arrival is coincident with the extinction of several species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mekosuchus" title="Mekosuchus">land crocodile</a> (<i>Mekosuchus kalpokasi</i>), <a href="/wiki/Meiolania" title="Meiolania">land tortoise</a> (<i>Meiolania damelipi</i>) and various flightless bird species.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> Lapita settlements reached as far east as <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> at their greatest extent.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Over time, the Lapita culture lost much of its early unity; as such, it became increasingly fragmented. The precise reasons for this are unclear. However, over the centuries pottery, settlement and burial practices in Vanuatu all evolved in a more localised direction, with long-distance trade and migration patterns contracting.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> However some limited long-distance trade did continue, with similar cultural practices and late-period items also being found in <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, the Bismarks and the Solomons.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> Finds in central and southern Vanuatu, such as distinctive adzes, also indicate some trade connections with, and possibly population movements of, Polynesian peoples to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Over time it is thought that the Lapita either mixed with, or acted as pioneers for, migrants coming from the Bismarks and elsewhere in Melanesia, ultimately producing the darker-skinned physiognomy that is typical of modern ni-Vanuatu.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> Linguistically, however, the Lapita peoples' Austronesian languages were maintained, with all of the numerous 100+ autochthonous <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Vanuatu" title="Languages of Vanuatu">languages of Vanuatu</a> being classified as belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanic</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_language_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian language family">Austronesian language family</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eth_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eth-22">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This linguistic hyperdiversity resulted from a number of factors: continuing waves of migration, the existence of numerous decentralised and generally self-sufficient communities, hostilities between people groups, with none able to dominate any of the others, and the difficult geography of Vanuatu that impeded inter- and intra-island travel and communication.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> The geological record also shows that a huge volcanic eruption occurred on <a href="/wiki/Ambrym" title="Ambrym">Ambrym</a> in circa 200 AD and on <a href="/wiki/Kuwae" title="Kuwae">Kuwae</a> in c. 1452â53 AD, which would have devastated local populations and likely resulted in further population movements.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kuwae2006_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kuwae2006-24">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Arrival_of_Europeans_.281606.E2.80.931906.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_of_Europeans_(1606â1906)">Arrival of Europeans (1606â1906)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Arrival of Europeans (1606â1906)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG/170px-Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG/255px-Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG/340px-Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1229" data-file-height="1335"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Quir%C3%B3s.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de QueirÃ³s">Pedro Fernandes de QueirÃ³s</a> was the first European to arrive in Vanuatu, in 1606. He named <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a>, the largest island in Vanuatu.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Vanuatu islands first had contact with Europeans in April 1606, when the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de QueirÃ³s">Pedro Fernandes de QueirÃ³s</a>, sailing for the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Crown</a>, sailed by the <a href="/wiki/Banks_Islands" title="Banks Islands">Banks Islands</a>, landing briefly on <a href="/wiki/Gaua" title="Gaua">Gaua</a> (which he called Santa MarÃ­a).<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jolly_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jolly-25">[24]</a></sup> Continuing further south, QueirÃ³s arrived at the largest island, naming it <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">La Austrialia del <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADritu_Santo" class="mw-redirect" title="EspÃ­ritu Santo">EspÃ­ritu Santo</a></i> or "The Southern Land of the Holy Spirit", believing he had arrived in <a href="/wiki/Terra_Australis" title="Terra Australis">Terra Australis</a> (Australia).<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> The Spanish established a short-lived settlement named <i>Nueva Jerusalem</i> at Big Bay on the north side of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jolly_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jolly-25">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Relations with the Ni-Vanuatu were initially friendly, though due to poor treatment of the local people by the Spanish, the situation soon soured and turned violent.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup> Much of the crew, including QueirÃ³s, were also suffering from ill health, with QueirÃ³s's mental state also deteriorating.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jolly_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jolly-25">[24]</a></sup> The settlement was abandoned after a month, with QueirÃ³s continuing his search for the southern continent.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Europeans did not return until 1768, when the French explorer <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine_de_Bougainville" title="Louis Antoine de Bougainville">Louis Antoine de Bougainville</a> sailed by the islands on 22 May, naming them the Great <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">Cyclades</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Anne_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anne-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup> Of the various French toponyms Bougainville devised, only <a href="/wiki/Pentecost_Island" title="Pentecost Island">Pentecost Island</a> has stuck.<sup id="cite_ref-Jolly_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jolly-25">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French landed on <a href="/wiki/Ambae" class="mw-redirect" title="Ambae">Ambae</a>, trading with the native people in a peaceful manner, though Bougainville stated that they were later attacked, necessitating him to fire warning shots with his muskets, before his crew left and continued their voyage.<sup id="cite_ref-Jolly_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jolly-25">[24]</a></sup> In JulyâSeptember 1774 the islands were explored extensively by British explorer <a href="/wiki/Captain_James_Cook" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain James Cook">Captain James Cook</a>, who named them the New Hebrides, after the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a> off the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, a name that lasted until independence in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jolly_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jolly-25">[24]</a></sup> Cook managed to maintain generally cordial relations with the Ni-Vanuatu by giving them presents and refraining from violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jolly_25-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jolly-25">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1789 <a href="/wiki/William_Bligh" title="William Bligh">William Bligh</a> and the remainder of his crew sailed through the Banks Islands on their return voyage to <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a> following the '<a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty">Mutiny on the Bounty</a>'; Bligh later returned to the islands, naming them after his benefactor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Banks" title="Joseph Banks">Joseph Banks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Whaleships were among the first regular visitors to this group of islands. The first recorded visit was by the <i>Rose</i> in February 1804, and the last known visit by the New Bedford ship <i>John and Winthrop</i> in 1887.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> In 1825, the trader <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dillon" title="Peter Dillon">Peter Dillon</a>'s discovery of <a href="/wiki/Sandalwood" title="Sandalwood">sandalwood</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Erromango" title="Erromango">Erromango</a>, highly valued as an incense in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> where it could be traded for tea, resulted in rush of incomers that ended in 1830 after a clash between immigrant Polynesian workers and indigenous Ni-Vanuatu.<sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sandalwood_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sandalwood-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198712-14_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198712-14-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Further sandalwood trees were found on Efate, Espiritu Santo, and Aneityum, prompting a series of boom and busts, though supplies were essentially exhausted by the mid-1860s, and the trade largely ceased.<sup id="cite_ref-Sandalwood_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sandalwood-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 1860s, <a href="/wiki/Plantations" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantations">planters</a> in Australia, Fiji, New Caledonia, and the Samoan islands, in need of labourers, encouraged a long-term <a href="/wiki/Indentured_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured labour">indentured labour</a> trade called "<a href="/wiki/Blackbirding" title="Blackbirding">blackbirding</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> At the height of the labour trade, more than one-half the adult male population of several of the islands worked abroad. Because of this, and the poor conditions and abuse often faced by workers, as well the introduction of common diseases to which native Ni-Vanuatu had no immunity, the population of Vanuatu declined severely, with the current population being greatly reduced compared to pre-contact times.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Archaeology_13-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archaeology-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Greater oversight of the trade saw it gradually wind down, with Australia barring any further 'blackbird' labourers in 1906, followed by Fiji and Samoa in 1910 and 1913 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides,_by_William_Hodges.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg/300px-The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg/450px-The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg/600px-The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides%2C_by_William_Hodges.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1876" data-file-height="932"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Landing_at_Tana_one_of_the_New_Hebrides,_by_William_Hodges.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> landing at <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna island</a>, c. 1774
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From 1839 onwards <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, arrived on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> At first they faced hostility, most notably with the killings of <a href="/wiki/John_Williams_(missionary)" title="John Williams (missionary)">John Williams</a> and James Harris of the <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">London Missionary Society</a> on Erromango in 1839.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198715_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198715-34">[33]</a></sup> Despite this they pressed on, resulting in many conversions; however, to the consternation of the European, this was often only skin-deep, with Ni-Vanuatu syncretising Christianity with traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Kastom" title="Kastom">kastom</a></i> beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The Anglican <a href="/wiki/Melanesian_Mission" title="Melanesian Mission">Melanesian Mission</a> also took promising young converts for further training in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup> Presbyterian missionaries proved particularly successful on Aneityum, though less so on Tanna, with missionaries being repeatedly chased off the island by locals throughout the 1840sâ60s.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup> The hostile response may have been partly to blame with the waves of illnesses and deaths the missionaries inadvertently brought with them.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other European settlers also came, looking for land for <a href="/wiki/Cotton_plantation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotton plantation">cotton plantations</a>, the first of these being Henry Ross Lewin on Tanna in 1865 (which he later abandoned).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198719_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198719-35">[34]</a></sup> When international cotton prices collapsed after the ending of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, they switched to coffee, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a>, bananas, and, most successfully, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a>. Initially British subjects from Australia made up the majority of settlers, however with little support from the British government they frequently struggled to make a success of their settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>French planters also began arriving, beginning with Ferdinand Chevillard on Efate in 1880, and later in larger numbers following the creation of the <i>Compagnie Caledonienne des Nouvelles-HÃ©brides</i> (CCNH) by John Higginson in 1882 (a fiercely pro-French Irishman), which soon tipped the balance in favour of French subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaUSA2009_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaUSA2009-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198726-7_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_Trease198726-7-37">[36]</a></sup> The French government took over the CCNH in 1894 and actively encouraged French settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> By 1906 French settlers (at 401) outnumbered the British (228) almost two to one.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Colonial_era_.281906.E2.80.931980.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era_(1906â1980)">Colonial era (1906â1980)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Colonial era (1906â1980)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides" title="New Hebrides">New Hebrides</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span id="Early_period_.281906.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_period_(1906â1945)">Early period (1906â1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early period (1906â1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Native_men_of_Tanna,_New_Hebrides.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Native_men_of_Tanna%2C_New_Hebrides.jpg/220px-Native_men_of_Tanna%2C_New_Hebrides.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Native_men_of_Tanna%2C_New_Hebrides.jpg/330px-Native_men_of_Tanna%2C_New_Hebrides.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Native_men_of_Tanna%2C_New_Hebrides.jpg/440px-Native_men_of_Tanna%2C_New_Hebrides.jpg 2x" data-file-width="730" data-file-height="460"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Native_men_of_Tanna,_New_Hebrides.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tanna men on a boat, taken c. 1905
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The jumbling of French and British interests in the islands and the near lawlessness prevalent there brought petitions for one or another of the two powers to annex the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The Convention of 16 October 1887 established a <a href="/wiki/Anglo-French_Joint_Naval_Commission" title="Anglo-French Joint Naval Commission">joint naval commission</a> for the sole purpose of protecting French and British citizens, with no claim to jurisdiction over internal native affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BresnihanWoodward2002_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BresnihanWoodward2002-38">[37]</a></sup> Hostilities between settlers and Ni-Vanuatu were commonplace, often centring on disputes over land which had been purchased in dubious circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> There was pressure from French settlers in New Caledonia to annex the islands, though Britain was unwilling to relinquish their influence completely.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginning_15-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginning-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result, in 1906 France and the United Kingdom agreed to administer the islands jointly; called the Anglo-French <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">Condominium</a>, it was a unique form of government, with two separate governmental, legal, judicial and financial systems that came together only in a (weak and ineffective) Joint Court.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Museum_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museum-39">[38]</a></sup> Land expropriation and exploitation of Ni-Vanuatu workers on plantations continued apace however.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> In an effort to curb the worst of the abuses, and with the support of the missionaries, the Condominium's authority was extended via the Anglo-French Protocol of 1914, although this was not formally ratified until 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Whilst this resulted in some improvements, labour abuses continued and Ni-Vanuatu were barred from acquiring the <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a> of either power, being officially stateless.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The underfunded Condominium government proved dysfunctional, with the duplication of administrations making effective governance difficult and time-consuming.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Education, healthcare and other such services were left in the hands of the missionaries.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 1920sâ30s, indentured workers from <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (then part of <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a>) came to work in the plantations in the New Hebrides.<sup id="cite_ref-Calnitsky_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calnitsky-40">[39]</a></sup> By 1929 there were some 6,000 Vietnamese people in the New Hebrides.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Calnitsky_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calnitsky-40">[39]</a></sup> There was some social and political unrest among them in the 1940s due to the poor working conditions and the social effects of Allied troops, who were generally more sympathetic to their plight than the planters.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> Most Vietnamese were repatriated in 1946 and 1963, though a small Vietnamese community remains in Vanuatu today.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg/220px-F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg/330px-F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg/440px-F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1928" data-file-height="1517"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:F6F-3_Hellcats_of_VF-40_at_Espiritu_Santo_1944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>US Navy <a href="/wiki/Grumman_F6F_Hellcat" title="Grumman F6F Hellcat">Hellcats</a> on <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a> island in February 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> brought immense change to the archipelago. The <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of France">fall of France</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> in 1940 allowed Britain to gain a level of greater authority on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Museum_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museum-39">[38]</a></sup> The Australian military stationed a 2,000-strong force on Malakula in a bid to protect Australia from a possible Japanese invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-Museum_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museum-39">[38]</a></sup> Following the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Attack on Pearl Harbour">attack on Pearl Harbour</a> on 7 December 1941 the United States joined the war on the Allied side; <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> soon advanced rapidly throughout Melanesia and was in possession of much of what is now Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands by April 1942, leaving the New Hebrides on the frontline of any further advance.<sup id="cite_ref-Museum_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Museum-39">[38]</a></sup> In order to forestall this, from May 1942 US troops were stationed on the islands, where they built airstrips, roads, military bases on Efate and Espiritu Santo, and an array of other supporting infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-LL_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LL-43">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the peak of the deployment some 50,000 Americans were stationed on the two military bases, outnumbering the native population of roughly 40,000, with thousands more Allied troops passing through the islands at some point.<sup id="cite_ref-LL_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LL-43">[42]</a></sup> A small Ni-Vanuatu force of some 200 men (the New Hebrides Defence Force) was established to support the Americans, and thousands more were engaged in construction and maintenance work as part of the <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_Labor_Corps" title="Vanuatu Labor Corps">Vanuatu Labor Corps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LL_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LL-43">[42]</a></sup> The American presence effectively sidelined the Anglo-French authorities for the duration of their stay, with the American's more tolerant and friendly attitude to the Ni-Vanuatu, informal habits, relative wealth, and the presence of African-American troops serving with a degree of equality (albeit in a <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States_Armed_Forces" title="Racial segregation in the United States Armed Forces">segregated force</a>) seriously undermining the underlying ethos of colonial superiority.<sup id="cite_ref-LL_43-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LL-43">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With the successful <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_campaign" title="Solomon Islands campaign">reoccupation of the Solomons</a> in 1943 the New Hebrides lost their strategic importance, and the Americans withdrew in 1945, selling much of their equipment at bargain prices and dumping the rest in the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The rapid American deployment and withdrawal led to growth in '<a href="/wiki/Cargo_cults" class="mw-redirect" title="Cargo cults">cargo cults</a>', most notably that of <a href="/wiki/John_Frum" title="John Frum">John Frum</a>, whereby Ni-Vanuatu hoped that by returning to traditional values whilst mimicking aspects of the American presence that 'cargo' (i.e. large quantities of American goods) would be delivered to them.<sup id="cite_ref-Guiart_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guiart-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-westoc_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-westoc-45">[44]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Condominium government returned, though understaffed and underfunded, it struggled to reassert its authority.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Lead-up_to_independence_.281945.E2.80.931980.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lead-up_to_independence_(1945â1980)">Lead-up to independence (1945â1980)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Lead-up to independence (1945â1980)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg/220px-Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg/330px-Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg/440px-Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_Hebrides.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1966 flag of the Anglo-French Condominium of the New Hebrides
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Decolonisation began sweeping the European empires after the war, and from the 1950s the Condominium government began a somewhat belated campaign of modernisation and economic development.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Hospitals were built, doctors trained and immunisation campaigns carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The inadequate mission-run school system was taken over and improved, with primary enrolment greatly increasing to be near-universal by 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> There was greater oversight of the plantations, with worker exploitation being clamped down on and Ni-Vanuatu paid higher wages.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New industries, such as <a href="/wiki/Cattle_ranching" class="mw-redirect" title="Cattle ranching">cattle ranching</a>, commercial fishing and <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a> mining were established.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Ni-Vanuatu began gradually to take over more positions of power and influence within the economy and the church.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Despite this the British and French still dominated the politics of the colony, with an Advisory Council set up in 1957 containing some Ni-Vanuatu representation having little power.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However the economic development brought with it unintended consequences. In the 1960s many planters began fencing off and clearing large areas of bushland for cattle ranching, which were often deemed to be communally-held <i>kastom</i> lands by Ni-Vanuatu.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> On Espiritu Santo the <a href="/wiki/Nagriamel" title="Nagriamel">Nagriamel</a> movement was founded in 1966 by Chief Buluk and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Stevens_(politician)" title="Jimmy Stevens (politician)">Jimmy Stevens</a> on a platform of opposing any further land clearances and gradual, Ni-Vanuatu-led, economic development.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> The movement gained a large following, prompting a crackdown by the authorities, with Buluk and Stevens being arrested in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Upon their release they began to press for complete independence.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> In 1971 Father <a href="/wiki/Walter_Lini" title="Walter Lini">Walter Lini</a> established another party â the New Hebrides Cultural Association, later renamed the <a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides_National_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="New Hebrides National Party">New Hebrides National Party</a> (NHNP) â also focused on achieving independent and opposition to land expropriation.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The NNDP first came to prominence in 1971, when the Condominium government was forced to intervene after a rash of land speculation by foreign nationals.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Meanwhile, French settlers, and Francophone and mixed-race Ni-Vanuatu, established two separate parties on a platform of more gradual political development â the <i>Mouvement Autonamiste des Nouvelles-HÃ©brides</i> (MANH), based on Espiritu Santo, and the <i>Union des CommunautÃ©s des Nouvelles-HÃ©brides</i> (UCNH) on Efate.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The parties aligned on linguistic and religious lines: the NHNP was seen as the party of Anglophone Protestants, and were backed by the British who wished to exit the colony altogether, whereas the MANH, UCNH, Nagriamel and others (collectively known as the 'Moderates') represented Catholic Francophone interests, and a more gradual path to independence.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> France backed these groups as they were keen to maintain their influence in the region, most especially in their mineral-rich colony of New Caledonia where they were attempting to suppress an independence movement.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PIM2_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIM2-47">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Meanwhile, economic development continued, with numerous banks and financial centres opening up in the early 1970s to take advantage of the territory's <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> status.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> A mini-building boom took off in Port Vila and, following the building of a deep-sea wharf, cruise ship tourism grew rapidly, with annual arrivals reaching 40,000 by 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The boom encouraged increasing urbanisation and the populations of Port Vila and <a href="/wiki/Luganville" title="Luganville">Luganville</a> grew rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Vemerana.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_Vemerana.svg/220px-Flag_of_Vemerana.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_Vemerana.svg/330px-Flag_of_Vemerana.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_Vemerana.svg/440px-Flag_of_Vemerana.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Vemerana.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Flag of the short-lived Republic of Vemarana
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In November 1974 the British and French met and agreed to create a Representative Assembly in the colony, based partly on universal suffrage and partly on appointed persons representing various interest groups.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/1975_New_Hebridean_general_election" title="1975 New Hebridean general election">election</a> took place in November 1975, resulting in an overall victory for the NHNP.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The Moderates disputed the results, with Jimmy Stevens threatening to secede and declare independence.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The Condominium's Resident Commissioners decided to postpone the opening of the Assembly, though the two sides proved unable to agree on a solution, prompting protests and counter-protests, some of which turned violent.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> After discussions and some fresh elections in disputed areas, the Assembly finally convened in November 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PIM5_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIM5-51">[50]</a></sup> The NHNP renamed itself the <a href="/wiki/Vanua%27aku_Pati" title="Vanua'aku Pati">Vanua'aku Pati</a> (VP) in 1977, and now supported immediate independence under a strong central government and an Anglicisation of the islands. The Moderates meanwhile supported a more gradual transition to independence and a federal system, plus the maintenance of French as an official language.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 1977 a joint Anglo-French and Ni-Vanuatu conference was held in London, at which it was agreed to hold fresh Assembly elections and later an independence referendum in 1980; the VP boycotted the conference and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/1977_New_Hebridean_general_election" title="1977 New Hebridean general election">election</a> in November.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PIM_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIM-52">[51]</a></sup> They set up a parallel 'People's Provisional Government' which had de facto control of many areas, prompting violent confrontations with Moderates and the Condominium government.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VT_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VT-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A compromise was eventually brokered, a Government of National Unity formed under a new constitution, and fresh <a href="/wiki/1979_New_Hebridean_general_election" title="1979 New Hebridean general election">elections</a> held in November 1979, which the VP won with a comfortable majority. Independence was now scheduled for 30 July 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> Performing less well than expected, the Moderates disputed the results.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PIM3_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIM3-55">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tensions continued throughout 1980. Violent confrontations occurred between VP and Moderate supporters on several islands.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> On Espiritu Santo Nagriamel and Moderate activists under Jimmy Stevens, funded by the American <a href="/wiki/Libertarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Libertarian">libertarian</a> organisation <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Foundation" title="Phoenix Foundation">Phoenix Foundation</a>, took over the island's government in January and declared the independent Republic of Vemarana, prompting VP supporters to flee and the central government to institute a blockade.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> In May an abortive Moderate rebellion broke out on Tanna, in the course of which one of their leaders was shot and killed.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> The British and French sent in troops in July in a bid to forestall the Vemarana secessionists, however the French, still ambivalent about independence, effectively neutered the force, prompting a collapse of law and order on Espiritu Santo resulting in large scale looting.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independent_Vanuatu_.281980.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_Vanuatu_(1980âpresent)">Independent Vanuatu (1980âpresent)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Independent Vanuatu (1980âpresent)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The New Hebrides, now renamed Vanuatu, achieved independence as planned on 30 July 1980 under <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu" title="Prime Minister of Vanuatu">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Walter_Lini" title="Walter Lini">Walter Lini</a>, with a ceremonial <a href="/wiki/President_of_Vanuatu" title="President of Vanuatu">President</a> replacing the Resident Commissioners.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShears1980_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShears1980-57">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cp_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-28">[27]</a></sup> The Anglo-French forces withdrew in August, and Lini called in troops from <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, sparking the brief '<a href="/wiki/Coconut_War" title="Coconut War">Coconut War</a>' against <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Stevens_(politician)" title="Jimmy Stevens (politician)">Jimmy Stevens</a>'s Vemarana separatists.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UCA_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCA-59">[58]</a></sup> The PNG forces quickly quelled the Vemarana revolt and Stevens surrendered on 1 September; he was later jailed.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_33-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Lini remained in office until 1991, running an Anglophone-dominated government and winning both the <a href="/wiki/1983_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="1983 Vanuatuan general election">1983</a> and <a href="/wiki/1987_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="1987 Vanuatuan general election">1987</a> elections.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In foreign affairs Lini joined the <a href="/wiki/Non_Aligned_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Non Aligned Movement">Non Aligned Movement</a>, opposed <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">Apartheid</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and all forms of colonialism, established links with <a href="/wiki/Libya%E2%80%93Vanuatu_relations" title="LibyaâVanuatu relations">Libya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93Vanuatu_relations" title="CubaâVanuatu relations">Cuba</a>, and opposed the French presence in New Caledonia and their nuclear testing in <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HUFFER,_Elise_1993,_pp._272â282_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HUFFER,_Elise_1993,_pp._272â282-65">[64]</a></sup> Opposition to Lini's tight grip on power grew and in 1987, after he had suffered a stroke whilst on a visit to the United States, a section of the <a href="/wiki/Vanua%27aku_Pati" title="Vanua'aku Pati">Vanua'aku Pati</a> (VP) under <a href="/wiki/Barak_Sop%C3%A9" title="Barak SopÃ©">Barak SopÃ©</a> broke off to form a new party (the <a href="/wiki/Melanesian_Progressive_Party" title="Melanesian Progressive Party">Melanesian Progressive Party</a>, MPP), and an attempt was made by President <a href="/wiki/Ati_George_Sokomanu" title="Ati George Sokomanu">Ati George Sokomanu</a> to unseat Lini.<sup id="cite_ref-UCA_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCA-59">[58]</a></sup> This failed, and Lini became increasingly distrustful of his VP colleagues, firing anyone he deemed to be disloyal.<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One such person, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Kalpokas" title="Donald Kalpokas">Donald Kalpokas</a>, subsequently declared himself to be VP leader, splitting the party in two.<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup> On 6 September 1991 a vote of no confidence removed Lini from power;<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup> Kalpokas became Prime Minister, and Lini formed a new party, the <a href="/wiki/National_United_Party_(Vanuatu)" title="National United Party (Vanuatu)">National United Party</a> (NUP).<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UCA_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCA-59">[58]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the economy had entered a downturn, with foreign investors and foreign aid put off by Lini's flirtation with Communist states and tourist numbers down due to the political turmoil, compounded by a crash in the price of <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a>, Vanuatu's main export.<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup> As a result, the Francophone <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Moderate_Parties" title="Union of Moderate Parties">Union of Moderate Parties</a> (UMP) won the <a href="/wiki/1991_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="1991 Vanuatuan general election">1991 election</a>, but not with enough seats to form a majority. A coalition was thus formed with Lini's NUP, with the UMP's <a href="/wiki/Maxime_Carlot_Korman" title="Maxime Carlot Korman">Maxime Carlot Korman</a> becoming Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since then Vanuatuan politics have been unstable, seeing a series of fractious coalition governments and the use of no confidence votes resulting in frequent changes of prime ministers. However, the democratic system as a whole has been maintained and Vanuatu remains a peaceful and reasonably prosperous state. Throughout most of the 1990s the UMP were in power, the prime ministership switching between UMP rivals Korman and <a href="/wiki/Serge_Vohor" title="Serge Vohor">Serge Vohor</a>, and the UMP instituting a more free market approach to the economy, cutting the public sector, improving opportunities for Francophone Ni-Vanuatu and renewing ties with France.<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> The government struggled however with splits within their NUP coalition partner and a series of strikes within the Civil Service in 1993â4, the latter dealt with by a wave of firings.<sup id="cite_ref-Steeves_63-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steeves-63">[62]</a></sup> Financial scandals dogged both Korman and Vohor, with the latter implicated in a scheme to sell <a href="/wiki/Vanuatuan_passport" class="mw-redirect" title="Vanuatuan passport">Vanuatuan passports</a> to foreigners.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FH_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-68">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1996 Vohor and President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_L%C3%A9y%C3%A9" title="Jean-Marie LÃ©yÃ©">Jean-Marie LÃ©yÃ©</a> were briefly abducted by the <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_Mobile_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Vanuatu Mobile Force">Vanuatu Mobile Force</a> over a pay dispute and later released unharmed.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UCA_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCA-59">[58]</a></sup> A riot occurred in Port Vila in 1998 when savers attempted to withdraw funds from the <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_National_Provident_Fund" title="Vanuatu National Provident Fund">Vanuatu National Provident Fund</a> following allegations of financial impropriety, prompting the government to declare a brief state of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-UCA_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCA-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FH_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-68">[67]</a></sup> A Comprehensive Reform Program was enacted in the 1998 with the aim of improving economic performance and cracking down on government corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-68">[67]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1998_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="1998 Vanuatuan general election">1998 Vanuatuan general election</a> the UMP were unseated by the VP under Donald Kalpokas.<sup id="cite_ref-UCA_59-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCA-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-M_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M-70">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-N_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-N-71">[70]</a></sup> However Kalpokas lasted only a year, resigning when threatened with a no confidence vote, being replaced by Barak SopÃ© of the MPP in 1999, who himself was unseated in a confidence vote in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FH_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-68">[67]</a></sup> Despite the political uncertainty Vanuatu's economy continued to grow in this period, fuelled by high demand for Vanuatu beef, tourism, remittances from foreign workers, and large aid packages from the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> (in 1997) and the US <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Challenge_Corporation" title="Millennium Challenge Corporation">Millennium Challenge</a> fund (in 2005).<sup id="cite_ref-LP_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LP-73">[72]</a></sup> Vanuatu was removed from the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> list of 'uncooperative tax havens' in 2003 and joined the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-LP_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LP-73">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-74">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg/220px-Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg/330px-Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg/440px-Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1367"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Devastation_after_Cyclone_Pam_14_March_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Devastation caused by Cyclone Pam in 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Edward_Natapei" title="Edward Natapei">Edward Natapei</a> of the VP became Prime Minister in 2001 and went on to win the <a href="/wiki/2002_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="2002 Vanuatuan general election">2002 Vanuatuan general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2004_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="2004 Vanuatuan general election">2004 Vanuatuan general election</a> saw Vohor and the UMP return to power, however Vohor lost much support over a secret deal to recognise <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">China-Taiwan dispute</a> and was unseated in a confidence vote less than five months after taking office, being replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ham_Lini" class="mw-redirect" title="Ham Lini">Ham Lini</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Appeal_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Appeal-77">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> Lini switched back recognition to the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> and the PRC remains a major aid donor to the Vanuatu government.<sup id="cite_ref-smh_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smh-79">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iht_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iht-80">[79]</a></sup> In 2007 violent clashes broke out in Port Vila between migrants from Tanna and Ambrym, in which two people died.<sup id="cite_ref-rnzi_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rnzi-81">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-74">[73]</a></sup> Lini lost the <a href="/wiki/2008_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="2008 Vanuatuan general election">2008 Vanuatuan general election</a>, with Natapei returning to power, however Vanuatu politics then entered a period of turmoil. There were frequent attempts by the opposition to unseat Natapei via the use of no confidence votes â though unsuccessful, he was briefly removed on a procedural technicality in November 2009, an action that was then overturned by the Chief Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sato_Kilman" title="Sato Kilman">Sato Kilman</a> of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Progressive_Party_(Vanuatu)" title="People's Progressive Party (Vanuatu)">People's Progressive Party</a> (PPP) managed to oust Natapei in another confidence vote in December 2010, only to be removed in the same manner himself by Vohor's UMP in April 2011, however the latter was deemed invalid on a technical point and Kilman returned as PM. However the Chief Justice then overturned Kilman's victory, with Natapei returning to power for 10 days, at which point the Parliament voted in Kilman once more.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> Kilman managed to remain in office for two years, before being ousted in March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> The new government was the first time the <a href="/wiki/Green_Confederation" title="Green Confederation">Green Confederation</a> was in power, and the new Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Moana_Carcasses_Kalosil" title="Moana Carcasses Kalosil">Moana Carcasses Kalosil</a>, was the first non Ni-Vanuatu to hold the position (Kalosil is of mixed French-Tahitian ancestry and a naturalised Vanuatu citizen). Kalosil instituted a review of the sale of diplomatic passports and publicly declared his support for the <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">West Papua</a> independence movement, a move supported by former PMs Kilman and Carlot Korman.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> Kalosil was ousted in yet another confidence vote in 2014, with the VP returning under <a href="/wiki/Joe_Natuman" title="Joe Natuman">Joe Natuman</a>, who himself was ousted the following year in a confidence vote led by Kilman, angered at being fired from his position of Foreign Affairs Minister. Meanwhile, the country was devastated by <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Pam" title="Cyclone Pam">Cyclone Pam</a> in 2015, which resulted in 16 deaths and enormous destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-16Deaths_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16Deaths-90">[89]</a></sup> A corruption investigation in 2015 resulted in the conviction of numerous MPs in Kilman's government for bribery, including former PM Moana Carcasses Kalosil.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> His authority severely weakened, Kilman lost the <a href="/wiki/2016_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="2016 Vanuatuan general election">2016 Vanuatuan general election</a> to <a href="/wiki/Charlot_Salwai" title="Charlot Salwai">Charlot Salwai</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Reunification_Movement_for_Change" title="Reunification Movement for Change">Reunification Movement for Change</a> (RMC). Salwai in turn lost the <a href="/wiki/2020_Vanuatuan_general_election" title="2020 Vanuatuan general election">2020 Vanuatuan general election</a> amidst allegations of perjury, bringing back in the VP under <a href="/wiki/Bob_Loughman" title="Bob Loughman">Bob Loughman</a> as the country dealt with the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Harold" title="Cyclone Harold">Cyclone Harold</a> and the global <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2020Guardian_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020Guardian-93">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Vanuatu was one of the last places on Earth to have avoided a coronavirus outbreak, recording its first case of COVID-19 in November 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Vanuatu" title="Geography of Vanuatu">Geography of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Vanuatu_map.png/220px-Vanuatu_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="479" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/Vanuatu_map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="716"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Vanuatu with its capital <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a>, located on its third largest island.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rentapau_-_The_Wildflowers_garden_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rentapau â The Wildflowers garden
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Vanuatu is a Y-shaped archipelago consisting of about 83 relatively small, geologically newer islands of <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic origin</a> (65 of them inhabited), with about 1,300 kilometres (810&nbsp;mi) between the most northern and southern islands.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> Two of these islands (<a href="/wiki/Matthew_and_Hunter_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Matthew and Hunter Islands">Matthew and Hunter</a>) are also claimed and controlled by France as part of the French <a href="/wiki/Sui_generis_collectivity" class="mw-redirect" title="Sui generis collectivity">collectivity</a> of New Caledonia. The country lies between latitudes 13Â°S and 21Â°S and longitudes 166Â°E and 171Â°E. </p>
