      <p>The fourteen of Vanuatu's islands that have surface areas of more than 100 square kilometres (39&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) are, from largest to smallest: <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malakula" title="Malakula">Malakula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Efate" title="Efate">Efate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erromango" title="Erromango">Erromango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambrym" title="Ambrym">Ambrym</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecost_Island" title="Pentecost Island">Pentecost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epi_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Epi (island)">Epi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambae" class="mw-redirect" title="Ambae">Ambae</a> or Aoba, <a href="/wiki/Gaua" title="Gaua">Gaua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanua_Lava" title="Vanua Lava">Vanua Lava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maewo" title="Maewo">Maewo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malo_Island" title="Malo Island">Malo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aneityum" title="Aneityum">Aneityum</a> or Anatom. The nation's largest towns are the capital <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a>, on Efate, and <a href="/wiki/Luganville" title="Luganville">Luganville</a> on Espiritu Santo.<sup id="cite_ref-State_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State-98">[97]</a></sup> The highest point in Vanuatu is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Tabwemasana" title="Mount Tabwemasana">Mount Tabwemasana</a>, at 1,879 metres (6,165&nbsp;ft), on the island of Espiritu Santo. </p>
      <p>Vanuatu's total area is roughly 12,274 square kilometres (4,739&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> of which its land surface is very limited (roughly 4,700 square kilometres (1,800&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)). Most of the islands are steep, with unstable soils and little permanent fresh water.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> One estimate, made in 2005, is that only 9% of land is used for agriculture (7% with permanent crops, plus 2% considered arable).<sup id="cite_ref-SOPAC_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOPAC-100">[99]</a></sup> The shoreline is mostly rocky with fringing reefs and no <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a>, dropping rapidly into the ocean depths.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are several active <a href="/wiki/Volcanoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanoes">volcanoes</a> in Vanuatu, including <a href="/wiki/Lopevi" title="Lopevi">Lopevi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Yasur" title="Mount Yasur">Mount Yasur</a> and several underwater volcanoes. <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_activity" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic activity">Volcanic activity</a> is common, with an ever-present danger of a major eruption; a nearby undersea eruption of 6.4 magnitude occurred in November 2008 with no casualties, and an eruption occurred in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Vanuatu is recognised as a distinct <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_ecoregion" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrestrial ecoregion">terrestrial ecoregion</a>, which is known as the <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_rain_forests" title="Vanuatu rain forests">Vanuatu rain forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-102">[101]</a></sup> It is part of the <a href="/wiki/Australasian_realm" title="Australasian realm">Australasian realm</a>, which includes New Caledonia, the Solomon Islands, Australia, New Guinea and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. </p>
      <p>Vanuatu's population (estimated in 2008 as growing 2.4% annually)<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> is placing increasing pressure on land and resources for agriculture, grazing, hunting, and fishing. 90% of Vanuatu households fish and consume fish, which has caused intense fishing pressure near villages and the depletion of near-shore fish species. While well-vegetated, most islands show signs of deforestation. The islands have been logged, particularly of high-value timber, subjected to wide-scale slash-and-burn agriculture, and converted to coconut plantations and cattle ranches, and now show evidence of increased soil erosion and landslides.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many upland watersheds are being deforested and degraded, and fresh water is becoming increasingly scarce. Proper waste disposal, as well as water and air pollution, are becoming troublesome issues around urban areas and large villages. Additionally, the lack of employment opportunities in industry and inaccessibility to markets have combined to lock rural families into a subsistence or self-reliance mode, putting tremendous pressure on local ecosystems.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.82/10, ranking it 18th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-104">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:708px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Port_Vila_aerial.jpg" class="image" title="The panorama of Port Vila, capital and largest city of Vanuatu."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Port_Vila_aerial.jpg/700px-Port_Vila_aerial.jpg" decoding="async" width="700" height="468" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e8/Port_Vila_aerial.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="685"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Port_Vila_aerial.jpg" title="File:Port Vila aerial.jpg"> </a>
         </div>The panorama of <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a>, capital and largest city of Vanuatu.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu_rain_forests" title="Vanuatu rain forests">Vanuatu rain forests</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG/220px-Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG/330px-Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG/440px-Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Tanna_Yasur.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cinder plain of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Yasur" title="Mount Yasur">Mount Yasur</a> on <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a> island.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Erakor_Beach,_Efate,_Vanuatu,_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Erakor_Beach%2C_Efate%2C_Vanuatu%2C_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/220px-Erakor_Beach%2C_Efate%2C_Vanuatu%2C_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Erakor_Beach%2C_Efate%2C_Vanuatu%2C_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/330px-Erakor_Beach%2C_Efate%2C_Vanuatu%2C_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Erakor_Beach%2C_Efate%2C_Vanuatu%2C_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/440px-Erakor_Beach%2C_Efate%2C_Vanuatu%2C_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3171" data-file-height="2219"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Erakor_Beach,_Efate,_Vanuatu,_2_June_2006_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Erakor Beach on <a href="/wiki/Efate" title="Efate">Efate</a> island.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite its tropical forests, Vanuatu has a limited number of plant and animal species. It has an indigenous flying fox, <i><a href="/wiki/Pteropus_anetianus" class="mw-redirect" title="Pteropus anetianus">Pteropus anetianus</a></i>. Flying foxes are important rainforest and timber regenerators. They pollinate and seed disperse a wide variety of native trees. Their diet is nectar, pollen and fruit and they are commonly called "fruit bats". They are in decline across their South Pacific range. However, governments are increasingly aware of the economic and ecological value of flying foxes and there are calls to increase their protection. There are no indigenous large mammals. </p>
      <p>The nineteen species of native reptiles include the <a href="/wiki/Ramphotyphlops_braminus" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramphotyphlops braminus">flowerpot snake</a>, found only on Efate. The <a href="/wiki/Fiji_banded_iguana" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiji banded iguana">Fiji banded iguana</a> (<i>Brachylophus fasciatus</i>) was introduced as a <a href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">feral</a> animal in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESprackland1992_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESprackland1992-105">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lp_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lp-106">[105]</a></sup> There are eleven species of bats (three unique to Vanuatu) and sixty-one species of land and water birds. While the small <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_rat" title="Polynesian rat">Polynesian rat</a> is thought to be indigenous, the large species arrived with Europeans, as did domesticated hogs, dogs, and cattle. The ant species of some of the islands of Vanuatu were catalogued by <a href="/wiki/E._O._Wilson" title="E. O. Wilson">E. O. Wilson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilson1994_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilson1994-107">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The region is rich in sea life, with more than 4,000 species of marine molluscs and a large diversity of <a href="/wiki/List_of_fishes_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="List of fishes of the Coral Sea">marine fishes</a>. Cone snails and stonefish carry poison fatal to humans. The <a href="/wiki/Achatina_fulica" title="Achatina fulica">Giant East African land snail</a> arrived only in the 1970s, but already has spread from the Port Vila region to Luganville. </p>
      <p>There are three or possibly four adult <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">saltwater crocodiles</a> living in Vanuatu's mangroves and no current breeding population.<sup id="cite_ref-lp_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lp-106">[105]</a></sup> It is said the crocodiles reached the northern part of the islands after cyclones, given the island chain's proximity to the Solomon Islands and New Guinea where crocodiles are very common.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Vanuatu" title="List of birds of Vanuatu">List of birds of Vanuatu</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Vanuatu" title="List of mammals of Vanuatu">List of mammals of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The climate is tropical, with about nine months of warm to hot rainy weather and the possibility of cyclones and three to four months of cooler, drier weather characterised by winds from the southeast. The water temperature ranges from 22&nbsp;Â°C (72&nbsp;Â°F) in winter to 28&nbsp;Â°C (82&nbsp;Â°F) in the summer. Cool between April and September, the days become hotter and more humid starting in October. The daily temperature ranges from 20â32&nbsp;Â°C (68â90&nbsp;Â°F). Southeasterly <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> occur from May to October.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Vanuatu has a long rainy season, with significant rainfall almost every month. The wettest and hottest months are December through April, which also constitutes the cyclone season. The driest months are June through November.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> Rainfall averages about 2,360 millimetres (93&nbsp;in) per year but can be as high as 4,000 millimetres (160&nbsp;in) in the northern islands.<sup id="cite_ref-SOPAC_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOPAC-100">[99]</a></sup> In 2015, the United Nations University gave Vanuatu the highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_disaster_risk" title="List of countries by natural disaster risk">natural disaster risk</a> of all the countries it measured.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_cyclones">Tropical cyclones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tropical cyclones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Pam#Vanuatu" title="Cyclone Pam">Cyclone Pam Â§&nbsp;Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.(%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.%28%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83%29.jpg/220px-%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.%28%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.%28%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83%29.jpg/330px-%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.%28%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.%28%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83%29.jpg/440px-%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.%28%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="433"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%90%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B0.(%D0%92%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Manaro_Voui" title="Manaro Voui">Manaro Voui</a>, the volcano on the island of <a href="/wiki/Ambae" class="mw-redirect" title="Ambae">Ambae</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In March 2015, <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Pam" title="Cyclone Pam">Cyclone Pam</a> impacted much of Vanuatu as a Category&nbsp;5 severe tropical cyclone, causing deaths and extensive damage to all the islands. As of 17&nbsp;March&nbsp;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the United Nations said the official death toll was 11 (six from <a href="/wiki/Efate" title="Efate">Efate</a> and five from <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a>), and 30&nbsp;were reported injured; these numbers were expected to rise as more remote islands reported back.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Vanuatu lands minister, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Regenvanu" title="Ralph Regenvanu">Ralph Regenvanu</a> said, "This is the worst disaster to affect Vanuatu ever as far as we know."<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-worst_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-worst-112">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In April 2020, <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Harold" title="Cyclone Harold">Cyclone Harold</a> roared through the Espiritu Santo town of Luganville, and caused great material damage there and on at least four islands.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Harold#Vanuatu" title="Cyclone Harold">Cyclone Harold Â§&nbsp;Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Vanuatu" title="List of earthquakes in Vanuatu">List of earthquakes in Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Vanuatu has relatively frequent earthquakes. Of the 58 M7 or greater events that occurred between 1909 and 2001, few were studied. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Vanuatu" title="Politics of Vanuatu">Politics of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Parliament,_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/300px-Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/450px-Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/600px-Vanuatu_Parliament%2C_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3167" data-file-height="2009"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Parliament,_Port_Vila_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Vanuatu's parliament
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of Vanuatu is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> with a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Vanuatu" title="Constitution of Vanuatu">written constitution</a>, which declares that the "head of the Republic shall be known as the President and shall symbolise the unity of the nation." The powers of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Vanuatu" title="President of Vanuatu">President of Vanuatu</a>, who is elected for a five-year term by a two-thirds vote of an electoral college, are primarily ceremonial.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> The electoral college consists of members of Parliament and the presidents of Regional Councils. The President may be removed by the electoral college for gross misconduct or incapacity. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu" title="Prime Minister of Vanuatu">Prime Minister</a>, who is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, is elected by a majority vote of a three-quarters <a href="/wiki/Quorum" title="Quorum">quorum</a> of the Parliament. The Prime Minister, in turn, appoints the Council of Ministers, whose number may not exceed a quarter of the number of parliamentary representatives. The Prime Minister and the Council of Ministers constitute the executive government. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Vanuatu" title="Parliament of Vanuatu">Parliament of Vanuatu</a> is <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> and has 52 members,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> who are elected by popular vote every four years unless earlier dissolved by a majority vote of a three-quarters quorum or by a directive from the President on the advice of the Prime Minister. The national Council of Chiefs, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Malvatu_Mauri" title="Malvatu Mauri">Malvatu Mauri</a></i> and elected by district councils of chiefs, advises the government on all matters concerning ni-Vanuatu culture and language. </p>
      <p>Besides national authorities and figures, Vanuatu also has high-placed people at the village level. Chiefs continue to be the leading figures at the village level. It has been reported that even politicians need to oblige them.<sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu-117">[116]</a></sup> One becomes such a figure by holding a number of lavish feasts (each feast allowing them a higher ceremonial grade) or alternatively through inheritance (the latter only in Polynesian-influenced villages). In northern Vanuatu, feasts are graded through the nimangki-system. </p>
      <p>Government and society in Vanuatu tend to divide along linguistic French and English lines. Forming <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition governments</a> has proved problematic at times, owing to differences between English and French speakers. Francophone politicians like those of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Moderate_Parties" title="Union of Moderate Parties">Union of Moderate Parties</a> tend to be conservative and support neo-liberal policies, as well as closer relations with France and the West. The anglophone <a href="/wiki/Vanua%27aku_Pati" title="Vanua'aku Pati">Vanua'aku Pati</a> identifies as socialist and anti-colonial. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Vanuatu" title="Supreme Court of Vanuatu">Supreme Court</a> consists of a chief justice and up to three other judges. Two or more members of this court may constitute a Court of Appeal. Magistrate courts handle most routine legal matters. The legal system is based on <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">British common law</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_civil_law" class="mw-redirect" title="French civil law">French civil law</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Vanuatu" title="Constitution of Vanuatu">constitution</a> also provides for the establishment of village or island courts presided over by chiefs to deal with questions of <a href="/wiki/Custom_(law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Custom (law)">customary law</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Squatting_in_Vanuatu" title="Squatting in Vanuatu">Squatting</a> occurs and the principle of <a href="/wiki/Adverse_possession" title="Adverse possession">adverse possession</a> does not exist.<sup id="cite_ref-RC_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RC-118">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Vanuatu" title="Foreign relations of Vanuatu">Foreign relations of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu,_Mr._Sato_Kilman,_in_Jaipur_on_August_21,_2015._The_Union_Minister_for_External_Affairs_and_Overseas_Indian_Affairs,_Smt._Sushma_Swaraj_is_also_seen_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu%2C_Mr._Sato_Kilman%2C_in_Jaipur_on_August_21%2C_2015._The_Union_Minister_for_External_Affairs_and_Overseas_Indian_Affairs%2C_Smt._Sushma_Swaraj_is_also_seen_%281%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu%2C_Mr._Sato_Kilman%2C_in_Jaipur_on_August_21%2C_2015._The_Union_Minister_for_External_Affairs_and_Overseas_Indian_Affairs%2C_Smt._Sushma_Swaraj_is_also_seen_%281%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu%2C_Mr._Sato_Kilman%2C_in_Jaipur_on_August_21%2C_2015._The_Union_Minister_for_External_Affairs_and_Overseas_Indian_Affairs%2C_Smt._Sushma_Swaraj_is_also_seen_%281%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="1125"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Vanuatu,_Mr._Sato_Kilman,_in_Jaipur_on_August_21,_2015._The_Union_Minister_for_External_Affairs_and_Overseas_Indian_Affairs,_Smt._Sushma_Swaraj_is_also_seen_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Vanuatu Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Sato_Kilman" title="Sato Kilman">Sato Kilman</a> with Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a> in August 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Vanuatu has joined the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Agence_de_Coop%C3%A9ration_Culturelle_et_Technique" title="Agence de CoopÃ©ration Culturelle et Technique">Agence de CoopÃ©ration Culturelle et Technique</a></i>, <i>la <a href="/wiki/Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophonie">Francophonie</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. </p>
      <p>Since 1980, Australia, the United Kingdom, France and New Zealand have provided the bulk of Vanuatu's development aid. Direct aid from the UK to Vanuatu ceased in 2005 following the decision by the UK to no longer focus on the Pacific. </p>
      <p>More recently, new donors such as the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Challenge_Account" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Challenge Account">Millennium Challenge Account</a> (MCA) of the United States and the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> have been providing increased amounts of aid funding and loans. In 2005 the MCA announced that Vanuatu was one of the first 15 countries in the world selected to receive support â an amount of US$65&nbsp;million was given for the provision and upgrading of key pieces of <a href="/wiki/Public_infrastructure" title="Public infrastructure">public infrastructure</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Free_West_Papua_(3)_(Imagicity_548).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Free_West_Papua_%283%29_%28Imagicity_548%29.jpg/220px-Free_West_Papua_%283%29_%28Imagicity_548%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Free_West_Papua_%283%29_%28Imagicity_548%29.jpg/330px-Free_West_Papua_%283%29_%28Imagicity_548%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Free_West_Papua_%283%29_%28Imagicity_548%29.jpg/440px-Free_West_Papua_%283%29_%28Imagicity_548%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3642" data-file-height="2438"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Free_West_Papua_(3)_(Imagicity_548).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Free_Papua_Movement" title="Free Papua Movement">Free West Papua</a> concert in Vanuatu
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In March 2017, at the 34th regular session of the UN Human Rights Council, Vanuatu made a joint statement on behalf of some other Pacific nations raising human rights abuses in the <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a> or West Papua region, which has been part of Indonesia since 1963,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> and requested that the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights produce a report<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-121">[120]</a></sup> as more than 100,000 Papuans allegedly have died during decades of <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Indonesia rejected Vanuatu's allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-121">[120]</a></sup> In September 2017, at the <a href="/wiki/Seventy-second_session_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="Seventy-second session of the United Nations General Assembly">72nd Session of the UN General Assembly</a>, the Prime Ministers of Vanuatu, Tuvalu and the Solomon Islands once again raised human rights concerns in West Papua.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, newspaper reports from Australia indicated growing concern about the level of Chinese investment in Vanuatu, with over 50% of the country's debt of $440&nbsp;million owed to China.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Concern was focused on the possibility that China would use Vanuatu's potential inability to repay debt as leverage to bargain for control of, or a <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a> presence at <a href="/wiki/Luganville" title="Luganville">Luganville</a> Wharf. China loaned and funded the $114&nbsp;million redevelopment of the wharf, which has already been constructed, with the capacity to dock naval vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Vanuatu retains strong economic and cultural ties to Australia, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (in particular France), the UK and New Zealand. Australia now provides the bulk of external assistance, including the police force, which has a paramilitary wing.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Karen Bell is the new UK High Commissioner to Vanuatu. The UK High Commission to Vanuatu, located in Port Vila, was re-opened in the summer of 2019 as part of the UK Government's 'Pacific Uplift' strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> The British Friends of Vanuatu,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> based in London, provides support for Vanuatu visitors to the UK, and can often offer advice and contacts to persons seeking information about Vanuatu or wishing to visit, and welcomes new members (not necessarily resident in the UK) interested in Vanuatu. The association's Charitable Trust funds small scale assistance in the education and training sector. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Armed forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Vanuatu" title="Law enforcement in Vanuatu">Law enforcement in Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are two police wings: the <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Vanuatu" title="Law enforcement in Vanuatu">Vanuatu Police Force</a> (VPF) and the paramilitary wing, the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Vanuatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Vanuatu">Vanuatu Mobile Force</a> (VMF).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-129">[128]</a></sup> Altogether there were 547 police officers organised into two main police commands: one in Port Vila and one in Luganville.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-129">[128]</a></sup> In addition to the two command stations there were four secondary police stations and eight police posts. This means that there are many islands with no police presence, and many parts of islands where getting to a police post can take several days.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> There is no purely military expenditure.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> In 2017, Vanuatu signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Vanuatu" title="Provinces of Vanuatu">Provinces of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG/300px-Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG" decoding="async" width="300" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG/450px-Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="609"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Provinces.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Provinces of Vanuatu
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Vanuatu has been divided into six provinces since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> The names in English of all provinces are derived from the initial letters of their constituent islands: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Malampa_Province" title="Malampa Province">Malampa</a> (<b>Mal</b>akula, <b>Am</b>brym, <b>Pa</b>ama)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Penama_Province" title="Penama Province">Penama</a> (<b>Pen</b>tecost, <b>Am</b>bae, <b>Ma</b>ewo&nbsp;â in French: PÃ©nama)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sanma_Province" title="Sanma Province">Sanma</a> (<b>San</b>to, <b>Ma</b>lo)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Shefa_Province" title="Shefa Province">Shefa</a> (<b>Sh</b>epherds group, <b>Efa</b>te&nbsp;â in French: ShÃ©fa)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tafea_Province" title="Tafea Province">Tafea</a> (<b>T</b>anna, <b>A</b>niwa, <b>F</b>utuna, <b>E</b>rromango, <b>A</b>neityum&nbsp;â in French: TafÃ©a)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Torba_Province" title="Torba Province">Torba</a> (<b>Tor</b>res Islands, <b>Ba</b>nks Islands)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Provinces are autonomous units with their own popularly elected local parliaments known officially as provincial councils.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They collect local taxes and make by-laws in local matters like tourism, the provincial budget or the provision of some basic services.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They are headed by a chairman elected from among the members of the local parliaments and assisted by a secretary appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Civil_service_commission" title="Civil service commission">Public Service Commission</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Their executive arm consists of a provincial government headed by an executive officer who is appointed by the Prime Minister with the advice of the minister of local government.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The provincial government is usually formed by the party that has the majority in the provincial council and, like the national government, is advised in Ni-Vanuatu culture and language by the local council of chiefs. The provincial president is constitutionally a member of the electoral college that elects the President of Vanuatu.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The provinces are in turn divided into municipalities (usually consisting of an individual island) headed by a council and a mayor elected from among the members of the council.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Vanuatu" title="Economy of Vanuatu">Economy of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/350px-Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="350" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/525px-Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/700px-Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Vanuatu's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:PortVilaMarketHall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PortVilaMarketHall.jpg/220px-PortVilaMarketHall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PortVilaMarketHall.jpg/330px-PortVilaMarketHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PortVilaMarketHall.jpg/440px-PortVilaMarketHall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:PortVilaMarketHall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A market hall in Port Vila
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The four mainstays of the economy are agriculture, tourism, offshore <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cattle_raising" class="mw-redirect" title="Cattle raising">raising cattle</a>. Vanuatu sells citizenship for about $150,000, and its passports allow visa-free travel throughout Europe. With demand from the Chinese market booming, passport sales may now account for more than 30% of the country's revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> There is substantial fishing activity, although this industry does not bring in much foreign exchange. Exports include <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kava" title="Kava">kava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> and timber; and imports include machinery and equipment, foodstuffs, and fuels. In contrast, mining activity is very low. </p>
      <p>Although <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a> mining halted in 1978, there was an agreement in 2006 to export manganese already mined but not yet exported. The country has no known petroleum deposits. A small light-industry sector caters to the local market. Tax revenues come mainly from import duties and a 15% <a href="/wiki/Value_Added_Tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Value Added Tax">VAT</a> on goods and services. Economic development is hindered by dependence on relatively few commodity exports, vulnerability to natural disasters, and long distances between constituent islands and from main markets. </p>
      <p>Agriculture is used for consumption as well as for export. It provides a living for 65% of the population. In particular, production of copra and kava create substantial revenue. Many farmers have been abandoning cultivation of food crops, and use earnings from kava cultivation to buy food.<sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet:Vanuatu-117">[116]</a></sup> Kava has also been used in ceremonial exchanges between clans and villages.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Cocoa is also grown for foreign exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, the number of households engaged in fishing was 15,758, mainly for consumption (99%), and the average number of fishing trips was 3 per week.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> The tropical climate enables growing of a wide range of fruits and vegetables and spices, including <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watermelon" title="Watermelon">watermelons</a>, leaf spices, <a href="/wiki/Carrot" title="Carrot">carrots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radish" title="Radish">radishes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eggplant" title="Eggplant">eggplants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a> (both green and cured), <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">pepper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">cucumber</a> and many others.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> In 2007, the value (in terms of millions of <a href="/wiki/Vatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Vatu">vatu</a>&nbsp;â the official currency of Vanuatu), for agricultural products, was estimated for different products: kava (341&nbsp;million vatu), copra (195), cattle (135), crop gardens (93), cocoa (59), forestry (56), fishing (24) and <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> (12).<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Vanuatu banned all use of plastic bags and plastic straws, with more plastic items scheduled to be banned in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Tourism"></span> Tourism brings in much-needed foreign exchange. Vanuatu is widely recognised as one of the premier vacation destinations for scuba divers wishing to explore coral reefs of the South Pacific region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris2006_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris2006-145">[144]</a></sup> A further significant attraction to scuba divers is the wreck of the US ocean liner and converted troop carrier <i><a href="/wiki/SS_President_Coolidge" title="SS President Coolidge">SS President Coolidge</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Espiritu_Santo" title="Espiritu Santo">Espiritu Santo</a> island. Sunk during World War II, it is one of the largest shipwrecks in the world that is accessible for recreational diving. Tourism increased 17% from 2007 to 2008 to reach 196,134 arrivals, according to one estimate.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> The 2008 total is a sharp increase from 2000, in which there were only 57,000 visitors (of these, 37,000 were from Australia, 8,000 from New Zealand, 6,000 from New Caledonia, 3,000 from Europe, 1,000 from North America, 1,000 from Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> Tourism has been promoted, in part, by Vanuatu being the site of several reality-TV shows. The ninth season of the reality TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Survivor_(American_TV_series)" title="Survivor (American TV series)">Survivor</a></i> was filmed on Vanuatu, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Survivor:_Vanuatu" title="Survivor: Vanuatu">Survivor: Vanuatu</a>âIslands of Fire</i>. Two years later, Australia's <i><a href="/wiki/Australian_Survivor_(season_2)" title="Australian Survivor (season 2)">Celebrity Survivor</a></i> was filmed at the same location used by the US version. In mid-2002, the government stepped up efforts to boost tourism. </p>
      <p>Financial services are an important part of the economy. Vanuatu is a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> that until 2008 did not release account information to other governments or law-enforcement agencies. International pressure, mainly from Australia, influenced the Vanuatu government to begin adhering to international norms to improve transparency. In Vanuatu, there is no <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Withholding_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Withholding tax">withholding tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">inheritance tax</a>, or exchange control. Many international ship-management companies choose to flag their ships under the Vanuatu flag, because of the tax benefits and favourable labour laws (Vanuatu is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Maritime_Organization" title="International Maritime Organization">International Maritime Organization</a> and applies its international conventions). Vanuatu is recognised as a "<a href="/wiki/Flag_of_convenience" title="Flag of convenience">flag of convenience</a>" country.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> Several file-sharing groups, such as the providers of the <a href="/wiki/KaZaA" class="mw-redirect" title="KaZaA">KaZaA</a> network of <a href="/wiki/Sharman_Networks" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharman Networks">Sharman Networks</a> and the developers of <a href="/wiki/WinMX" title="WinMX">WinMX</a>, have chosen to incorporate in Vanuatu to avoid regulation and legal challenges. In response to foreign concerns the government has promised to tighten regulation of its <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial centre</a>. Vanuatu receives <a href="/wiki/Foreign_aid" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign aid">foreign aid</a> mainly from Australia and New Zealand. </p>
      <p>Vanuatu became the 185th member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">World Intellectual Property Organization</a> (WIPO) in December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Commercial_agriculture,_North_Efate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg/170px-Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg/255px-Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg/340px-Commercial_agriculture%2C_North_Efate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2340" data-file-height="3656"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Commercial_agriculture,_North_Efate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Commercial_agriculture" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial agriculture">Commercial agriculture</a>, North Efate
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Raising cattle leads to beef production for export. One estimate in 2007 for the total value of cattle heads sold was 135&nbsp;million vatu; cattle were first introduced into the area from Australia by British planter James Paddon.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> On average, each household has 5 pigs and 16 chickens, and while cattle are the "most important livestock", pigs and chickens are important for subsistence agriculture as well as playing a significant role in ceremonies and customs (especially pigs).<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> There are 30 commercial farms (sole proprietorships (37%), partnerships (23%), corporations (17%)), with revenues of 533&nbsp;million vatu and expenses of 329&nbsp;million vatu in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Earthquakes can negatively affect economic activity on the island nation. A severe earthquake in November 1999, followed by a <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a>, caused extensive damage to the northern island of <a href="/wiki/Pentecost_Island" title="Pentecost Island">Pentecost</a>, leaving thousands homeless. Another powerful earthquake in January 2002 caused extensive damage in the capital, Port Vila, and surrounding areas, and was also followed by a tsunami. Another earthquake of 7.2 struck on 2 August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS7.2_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS7.2-153">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Vanuatu National Statistics Office (VNSO) released their 2007 agricultural census in 2008. According to the study, agricultural exports make up about three-quarters (73%) of all exports; 80% of the population lives in rural areas where "agriculture is the main source of their livelihood"; and of these households, almost all (99%) engaged in agriculture, fisheries and forestry.<sup id="cite_ref-spc.int_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-154">[153]</a></sup> Total annual household income was 1,803&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Vatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Vatu">vatu</a>. Of this income, agriculture grown for their own household use was valued at 683&nbsp;million vatu, agriculture for sale at 561, gifts received at 38, handicrafts at 33 and fisheries (for sale) at 18.<sup id="cite_ref-spc.int_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spc.int-154">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The largest expenditure by households was food (300&nbsp;million vatu), followed by household appliances and other necessities (79&nbsp;million vatu), transportation (59), education and services (56), housing (50), alcohol and tobacco (39), clothing and footwear (17).<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> Exports were valued at 3,038&nbsp;million vatu, and included copra (485), kava (442), cocoa (221), beef (fresh and chilled) (180), timber (80) and fish (live fish, aquarium, shell, button) (28).<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> Total imports of 20,472&nbsp;million vatu included industrial materials (4,261), food and drink (3,984), machinery (3,087), consumer goods (2,767), transport equipment (2,125), fuels and lubricants (187) and other imports (4,060).<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> There are substantial numbers of crop gardens&nbsp;â 97,888 in 2007&nbsp;â many on flat land (62%), slightly hilly slope (31%), and even on steep slopes (7%); there were 33,570 households with at least one crop garden, and of these, 10,788 households sold some of these crops over a twelve-month period.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The economy grew about 6% in the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-Asian_Development_Bank_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asian_Development_Bank-159">[158]</a></sup> This is higher than in the 1990s, when GDP rose less than 3%, on average. </p>
      <p>One report from the <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> about Vanuatu's economy gave mixed reviews. It noted the economy was "expanding", noting that the economy grew at an impressive 5.9% rate from 2003 to 2007, and lauded "positive signals regarding reform initiatives from the government in some areas" but described certain binding constraints such as "poor infrastructure services". Since a private monopoly generates power, "electricity costs are among the highest in the Pacific" among developing countries. The report also cited "weak governance and intrusive interventions by the State" that reduced productivity.<sup id="cite_ref-Asian_Development_Bank_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asian_Development_Bank-159">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Vanuatu was ranked the 173rd safest investment destination in the world in the March 2011 Euromoney Country Risk rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> In 2015, Vanuatu was ranked the 84th most <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">economically free country</a> by The Heritage Foundation and <i>The Wall Street Journal</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Economic_Freedom_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economic_Freedom-161">[160]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Vanuatu" title="Telecommunications in Vanuatu">Telecommunications in Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Mobile phone service in the islands is provided by Vodafone (formerly TVL)<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a>. Internet access is provided by Vodafone, Telsat Broadband, <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a> and Wantok using a variety of connection technologies. A submarine optical fibre cable now connects Vanuatu to Fiji.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Vanuatu" title="Demographics of Vanuatu">Demographics of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Vanuatu_demography.png/350px-Vanuatu_demography.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Vanuatu_demography.png/525px-Vanuatu_demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Vanuatu_demography.png/700px-Vanuatu_demography.png 2x" data-file-width="724" data-file-height="426"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu_demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Vanuatu's population in thousands (1961â2003).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Landdiving7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Landdiving7.jpg/220px-Landdiving7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Landdiving7.jpg/330px-Landdiving7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Landdiving7.jpg/440px-Landdiving7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="690"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Landdiving7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Men wearing traditional <a href="/wiki/Namba_(clothing)" title="Namba (clothing)">nambas</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2009 census, Vanuatu has a population of 243,304.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_census_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_census-164">[163]</a></sup> Males outnumber females; in 1999, according to the Vanuatu Statistics Office, there were 95,682 males and 90,996 females.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The population is predominantly rural, but Port Vila and <a href="/wiki/Luganville" title="Luganville">Luganville</a> have populations in the tens of thousands. </p>
      <p>The inhabitants of Vanuatu are called <span class="nowrap"><i><a href="/wiki/Ni-Vanuatu" title="Ni-Vanuatu">ni-Vanuatu</a></i></span> in English, using a recent <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">coinage</a>. The ni-Vanuatu are primarily (98.5%) of <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesian</a> descent, with the remainder made up of a mix of Europeans, Asians and other Pacific islanders. Three islands were historically colonised by <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_outlier" title="Polynesian outlier">Polynesians</a>. About 20,000 <span class="nowrap">ni-Vanuatu</span> live and work in New Zealand and Australia. In 2006 the <a href="/wiki/New_Economics_Foundation" title="New Economics Foundation">New Economics Foundation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Earth" title="Friends of the Earth">Friends of the Earth</a> environmentalist group published the <a href="/wiki/Happy_Planet_Index" title="Happy Planet Index">Happy Planet Index</a>, which analysed data on <a href="/wiki/Subjective_life_satisfaction" class="mw-redirect" title="Subjective life satisfaction">levels of reported happiness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecological_Footprint" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecological Footprint">Ecological Footprint</a>, and they estimated Vanuatu to be the most ecologically efficient country in the world in achieving high well-being.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Trade in citizenship for investment has been an increasingly significant revenue earner for Vanuatu in recent years. The sale of what is called "honorary citizenship" in Vanuatu has been on offer for several years under the Capital Investment Immigration Plan and more recently the Development Support Plan. People from mainland China make up the bulk of those who have purchased honorary citizenship, entitling them to a Vanuatu passport.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Vanuatu" title="Languages of Vanuatu">Languages of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The national language of the Republic of Vanuatu is <a href="/wiki/Bislama" title="Bislama">Bislama</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> are Bislama, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. The principal languages of education are English and French. The use of English or French as the formal language is split along political lines.<sup id="cite_ref-Francophonie_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Francophonie-167">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bislama is a <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a> spoken natively in urban areas. Combining a typical Melanesian grammar and phonology with an almost entirely English-derived vocabulary, Bislama is the <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the archipelago, used by the majority of the population as a second language. </p>
      <p>In addition, 113 <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Vanuatu" title="Languages of Vanuatu">indigenous languages</a>, all of which are <a href="/wiki/Southern_Oceanic_languages" title="Southern Oceanic languages">Southern Oceanic languages</a> except for three outlier <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian languages</a>, are spoken in Vanuatu.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-168">[167]</a></sup> The density of languages, per capita, is the highest of any nation in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowley2000_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowley2000-169">[168]</a></sup> with an average of only 2,000 speakers per language. All <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular</a> languages of Vanuatu (i.e., excluding Bislama) belong to the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanic</a> branch of the Austronesian family. </p>
      <p>In recent years, the use of Bislama as a first language has considerably encroached on indigenous languages, whose use in the population has receded from 73.1 to 63.2 percent between 1999 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFranÃ§ois2012104_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFranÃ§ois2012104-170">[169]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Vanuatu" title="Religion in Vanuatu">Religion in Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG/220px-Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG/330px-Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG/440px-Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Port-Vila_cath_Sacre_Coeur.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roman Catholic cathedral
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Christianity is the predominant <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Vanuatu" title="Religion in Vanuatu">religion in Vanuatu</a>, consisting of several denominations. About one-third of the population belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Vanuatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian Church in Vanuatu">Presbyterian Church in Vanuatu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> making Vanuatu the most Presbyterian country in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> are other common denominations, each claiming about 15% of the population. The less significant groups are the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Christ_in_Australia" title="Churches of Christ in Australia">Church of Christ</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neil_Thomas_Ministries" title="Neil Thomas Ministries">Neil Thomas Ministries</a> (NTM), <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, and others. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Vanuatu" title="Islam in Vanuatu">Islam in Vanuatu</a> was estimated to consist of about 200 converts.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of the modern goods that the military in the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> brought with them when they came to the islands, several <a href="/wiki/Cargo_cult" title="Cargo cult">cargo cults</a> developed. Many died out, but the <a href="/wiki/John_Frum" title="John Frum">John Frum</a> cult on <a href="/wiki/Tanna_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanna (island)">Tanna</a> is still large, and has adherents in the parliament.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Also on Tanna is the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Philip Movement">Prince Philip Movement</a>, which reveres the United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Philip">Prince Philip</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> Villagers of the <a href="/wiki/Yaohnanen" title="Yaohnanen">Yaohnanen</a> tribe believed in an ancient story about the pale-skinned son of a mountain spirit venturing across the seas to look for a powerful woman to marry. Prince Philip, having visited the island with his new wife <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, fitted the description exactly and is therefore revered as a god around the isle of Tanna.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> After Philip died, an anthropologist familiar with the group, said that after their period of mourning the group would probably transfer their veneration to Prince Charles, who had visited Vanuatu in 2018 and met with some of the tribal leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Vanuatu" title="Health in Vanuatu">Health in Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The estimated literacy rate of people aged 15â24 years is about 74% according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> figures.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> The rate of primary school enrolment rose from 74.5% in 1989 to 78.2% in 1999 and then to 93.0% in 2004 but then fell to 85.4% in 2007. The proportion of pupils completing a primary education fell from 90% in 1991 to 72% in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-179">[178]</a></sup> and up to 78% in 2012. </p>
      <p>Port Vila and three other centres have campuses of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">University of the South Pacific</a>, an educational institution co-owned by twelve Pacific countries. The campus in Port Vila, known as the Emalus Campus, houses the University's law school. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Vanuatu" title="Culture of Vanuatu">Culture of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu,_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG/170px-Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="297" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG/255px-Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG/340px-Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu%2C_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1796" data-file-height="3140"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wooden_slit_drums_from_Vanuatu,_Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Wooden <a href="/wiki/Slit_drum_(Vanuatu)" title="Slit drum (Vanuatu)">slit drums</a> from Vanuatu, <a href="/wiki/Bernice_P._Bishop_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernice P. Bishop Museum">Bernice P. Bishop Museum</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Vanuatu culture retains a strong diversity through local regional variations and through foreign influence. Vanuatu may be divided into three major cultural regions. In the north, wealth is established by how much one can give away, through a <a href="/wiki/Grade-taking" title="Grade-taking">grade-taking</a> system. Pigs, particularly those with rounded <a href="/wiki/Tusk" title="Tusk">tusks</a>, are considered a symbol of wealth throughout Vanuatu. In the centre, more traditional Melanesian cultural systems dominate. In the south, a system involving grants of title with associated privileges has developed.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-168">[167]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Young men undergo various coming-of-age ceremonies and rituals<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> to initiate them into manhood, usually including <a href="/wiki/Circumcision" title="Circumcision">circumcision</a>. </p>
      <p>Most villages have a <i><a href="/wiki/Nakamal" title="Nakamal">nakamal</a></i> or village clubhouse, which serves as a meeting point for men and a place to drink <i><a href="/wiki/Kava" title="Kava">kava</a></i>. Villages also have male- and female-only sections. These sections are situated all over the villages; in <i>nakamals</i>, special spaces are provided for females when they are in their menstruation period. </p>
      <p>There are few prominent ni-Vanuatu authors. <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">Women's rights</a> activist <a href="/wiki/Grace_Mera_Molisa" title="Grace Mera Molisa">Grace Mera Molisa</a>, who died in 2002, achieved international notability as a descriptive poet. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Vanuatu" title="Music of Vanuatu">Music of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
