        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A women's dance from Vanuatu, using bamboo stamping tubes." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg/220px-Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg/330px-Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg/440px-Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="2336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanuatu-humans-of-vanuatu-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A women's dance from Vanuatu, using <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_musical_instruments" title="Bamboo musical instruments">bamboo stamping tubes</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The traditional <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Vanuatu" title="Music of Vanuatu">music of Vanuatu</a> is still thriving in the rural areas of Vanuatu.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> Musical instruments consist mostly of <a href="/wiki/Idiophone" title="Idiophone">idiophones</a>: drums of various shape and size, <a href="/wiki/Slit_gong" class="mw-redirect" title="Slit gong">slit gongs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_musical_instruments" title="Bamboo musical instruments">stamping tubes</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Rattle_(percussion_instrument)" title="Rattle (percussion instrument)">rattles</a>, among others. Another musical genre that has become widely popular during the 20th century in all areas of Vanuatu, is known as <i><a href="/wiki/String_band" title="String band">string band</a></i> music. It combines guitars, <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">ukulele</a>, and popular songs. </p>
      <p>More recently the music of Vanuatu, as an industry, grew rapidly in the 1990s and several bands have forged a distinctive ni-Vanuatu identity.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> Popular genres of modern commercial music, which are currently being played in the urban areas include <a href="/wiki/Zouk_(musical_movement)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zouk (musical movement)">zouk</a> music and <a href="/wiki/Reggaeton" title="Reggaeton">reggaeton</a>. Reggaeton, a variation of Dancehall Reggae spoken in the Spanish language, played alongside its own distinctive beat, is especially played in the local nightclubs of Port Vila with, mostly, an audience of Westerners and tourists. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Vanuatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Vanuatu">Cuisine of Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Vanuatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Vanuatu">cuisine of Vanuatu</a> (<i>aelan kakae</i>) incorporates fish, root vegetables such as <a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, fruits, and vegetables. Most island families grow food in their gardens, and food shortages are rare. Papayas, pineapples, mangoes, <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, and sweet potatoes are abundant through much of the year. Coconut milk and coconut cream are used to flavour many dishes. Most food is cooked using hot stones or through boiling and steaming; very little food is fried.<sup id="cite_ref-pc_97-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-97">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The national dish of Vanuatu is the <a href="/wiki/Laplap" title="Laplap">laplap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Vanuatu" title="Sport in Vanuatu">Sport in Vanuatu</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most practiced sport in Vanuatu is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>. The top flight league is the <a href="/wiki/VFF_National_Super_League" title="VFF National Super League">VFF National Super League</a> while the <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila_Football_League" title="Port Vila Football League">Port Vila Football League</a> is another important competition. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The island of <a href="/wiki/Pentecost_Island" title="Pentecost Island">Pentecost</a> is known for its tradition of <a href="/wiki/Land_diving" title="Land diving">land diving</a>, locally known as <i>gol</i>. The ritual consists for men to land dive off a 98-foot-high wooden tower with their ankles tied to vines, as part of the annual <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yam</a> <a href="/wiki/Harvest_festival" title="Harvest festival">harvest festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> This local tradition is often compared to the modern practice of <a href="/wiki/Bungee_jumping" title="Bungee jumping">bungee jumping</a>, which developed in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> in the 1980s. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

        <li>
